However, the agricultural association and the education association have just received the organizational charter, and they must be reorganized before they can create a roster, submit it for review, which is extremely difficult in fact. Therefore, they hesitated a lot.

The Truth About the False Robbery Case: Zhu Guangxin, a policeman from the third sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau, is currently serving as a learning policeman in the second sub-bureau. When he was in Nanmen, he became acquainted with a Jingjiang woman, Liu Wang. Recently, she had an affair with Gu Hongquan, the brother-in-law who opened the Yichang Silk Factory, and gradually became estranged from Zhu. Recently, Zhu was dismissed from his job due to an incident. He was not only suffering from unemployment, but also from unrequited love, and he felt more bored. So he went to Gu Hongquan's house every day to tease Gu's wife, Gu Wang. The night before last, he saw Liu Wang going to Gu's house again, so he invited a friend to follow her to Gu's house, and teased Liu Wang and Gu Wang, asking to have fun. They were shocked and immediately grabbed Zhu and shouted for help, repeatedly calling for catching robbers. The neighbors gathered when they heard the sound, and Gu Hongquan also returned home from outside. They immediately twisted Zhu Guangxin and sent him to the third sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau. After interrogation, he was sent to the County Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Changshu 85

Local Thugs Secretly Investigate Over Two Hundred Pounds of Opium: At about 10:00 PM on the 2nd of this month, a large sand boat passed through the city river of Dayi Bridge Town in the Ninth District of this county. The cabin was empty, but the sand boat was drawing very deep, which was seen by local thugs. Knowing that there was something unusual, they agreed to follow it to a remote place at the end of the market, impersonated policemen, and ordered the ship to stop for inspection. The sand boat crew panicked when they heard the order, but they could not refuse, so they docked the boat. The thugs immediately jumped on the sand boat and found a large amount of opium at the bottom of the cabin. It was said that it weighed more than two hundred pounds. They immediately went ashore, and the sand boat also sailed elsewhere. Yesterday (the 5th), Fang Fengshao, the patrolling officer of the Tenth Sub-Bureau of the Public Security Bureau, got the news and immediately sent police to investigate secretly, but there was no clue. As a result, Officer Fang came to the city and reported to the General Bureau. Currently, detectives have been secretly sent to the countryside to investigate.

They have been ordered that, since they are currently in a period of pacification, if the Yan bandits can repent, they should surrender to the government.

Gaoyou 88

The Storm of Destroying City God Idols Has Been Resolved: The executive and supervisory committee members of the County Party Headquarters, in order to completely eliminate superstition, destroyed all the idols in the City God Temple, which aroused a backlash from various Taoist nuns. At about 6:00 PM on the 27th, they gathered people to destroy the County Party Headquarters and the residences of Party Committee members Huang Songtao and Huang Renyan. They also marched in the streets for several days, ordering shops to close. It is heard that the various Taoist nuns have now accepted this plan.

Baozhen Class Narrowly Escaped Bandit Robbery: At about 4:00 PM on the 2nd, at the Dragon King Temple in Luzhen, belonging to Yangzhou, thirty or forty bandits intercepted the Huo postal barge of the Dada Company and the Gao family fishing boat. On the 3rd, the bandits gathered more than a hundred people and intercepted the upstream small steamship of the Baozhen class of the Fuyun Company at a place twenty-five li from the county seat. Fortunately, there was a company of troops from the 94th Brigade of the Liang Ministry on board the ship, so they opened fire with the bandits. As a result, four officers and soldiers were injured, eight bandits were killed, and sixteen were captured alive. They have been sent to the Yangzhou Pacification Supervisory Office for handling according to law. Yesterday (the 4th) at 3:00 PM, the military and police agencies of this city held a special meeting and decided to impose a special curfew every day at 8:00 PM.

Yangzhong 89

Director of Education Bureau Maintains Method of Education Expenses: Due to the collection relationship, the education funds in Yangzhong County must feel very embarrassed every spring. Moreover, the county is remote and poor, and there is no money house to borrow from. The new Director of the Education Bureau, Fan Xuezhen, took office and happened to be at this difficult time. Therefore, Fan has formulated several methods: (1) Request the county government to continue to collect the unfinished universal education mu tax for the seventeenth year of the Republic. (2) Draft a temporary method for education fund relief. The general idea is to ask the county government to issue promissory notes worth three thousand yuan during these four months of difficulty, with a face value of one yuan each, allowing them to be used to pay off the busy periods above and below. The Education Bureau will then distribute five percent of the full salary (one thousand four hundred yuan per month) to each school on a monthly basis. The teachers and staff can make credit loans to parents and friends in the school's location to maintain themselves. When the busy periods above and below are collected, they will be repaid in installments over six months, with five hundred yuan being withdrawn each month from June to November. This can not only maintain the difficult situation for the first four months of the year, but also not hinder the various expenses for the second six months. (3) In addition to the promissory notes being issued at five percent, if the county government and the Education Bureau receive a certain amount of cash in the near future, they will distribute it to each school on a pro rata basis. (4) Regarding the school supplies for each school, the Education Bureau will purchase them on credit from bookstores in Zhenjiang and distribute them to each school for use. This will not only prevent the principals from embezzling private funds, but also allow the principals to collect cash from the students' parents to supplement the funds. (5) Actively pursue and collect any outstanding or unpaid rent from the Education Bureau's own property. The above are all methods in the absence of methods for education expenses, so as to avoid the principals' trekking to claim salaries affecting students' studies, and to ensure that schools and administration do not interfere with each other. It is now heard that the issuance of promissory notes has been approved by the county government meeting and is being submitted to the provincial government for review. Once approved, it can be realized.

Mingguang 90

Bandit Atmosphere Rampant in Eastern Anhui: Jiang Guochang's gang of bandits, entrenched on the border of Anhui and Dingyuan, previously fled into the territory of Liuhe. They were repulsed by the Xu Regiment of the Garrison Brigade and retreated back, entrenched in the Xiaohongshan area of the county. Recently, they have colluded with Mao Liu's and Fan's gangs from Sixian, totaling more than six hundred people, and the remnants of Ma Yuren's troops from Jiangbei, four to five hundred people, totaling more than two thousand people, with complete firearms and a great momentum. From the eastern border of Dingyuan, extending to the old Jiashan, Zhong Jiashan, Xiaohongshan, Zilaiqiao, and surrounding areas of Sanjie, more than a hundred li in circumference, have become areas where bandits gather. Jiang's gang and the remnants of Ma's troops gathered east of the railway, and Mao's and Fan's gangs gathered west of the railway, supporting each other. In recent days, they have captured more than thirty fortresses in Shangzhou, Dayue, and Yinshanji, abducting more than three hundred hostages and killing more than a hundred people. All the self-defense firearms were lost. Today, the bandits have approached the Xiaobian Village and Dagan Village area, only a few li away from Mingguang, and the townspeople are extremely panicked. In addition to the strict defense by the Wang Regiment of the 2nd Cavalry Division stationed there and the Self-Defense Corps, all public groups jointly telegraphed the headquarters and the provincial government, requesting that a large army be sent quickly to encircle and suppress them.

Education News

Important News

Guaranteeing Independent Funding for Education After the Abolition of Lilkin and Unified Salt Tax 91

▲ Local Customs Authorities to Allocate as Usual

｜Executive Yuan Orders Ministry of Finance to Handle｜

The Ministry of Education previously drafted measures to continue guaranteeing funding for education after the abolition of Lilkin and unified salt tax, and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for approval. The cases were approved by the governments of Anhui and Jiangsu provinces, and reports were received from the education departments of Jiangxi, Hunan, and Rehe provinces, as well as the education bureau of Beiping municipality. They stated that the central government's order to abolish Lilkin and unify the salt tax would greatly affect educational funding, and requested measures to maintain independence, etc. These were successively submitted to the ministry.

It is noted that our party's internal policy platform includes provisions for determining and guaranteeing the independence of educational funding. Furthermore, the ministry, with the approval of the Executive Yuan, issued a general order to all provinces and municipalities to strictly comply with this, and that the established local educational funding should not be arbitrarily altered. In recent years, various provinces and municipalities, in accordance with the provisions for the independence of educational funding in the political platform, have adopted appropriate measures, such as adding surcharges to salt taxes or allocating a portion of regular taxes as a fixed educational fund. Therefore, educational facilities in various provinces have made progress to varying degrees, except in special circumstances.

Now that the abolition of Lilkin has been implemented and salt tax surcharges are limited to unified collection by the Ministry of Finance from March 1, 1931, the fundamental foundation of the aforementioned educational fund is shaken. Although there is this surcharge, the original dedicated expenditure will be difficult to replenish in a short time. It is also stipulated that a factual report should be submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and referral to the Ministry of Finance to devise methods for allocating funds to subsidize it. However, there are still no concrete measures determined, and education departments and bureaus in various provinces and municipalities generally believe that the reduction in original educational funding due to the abolition of Lilkin or other factors is difficult to compensate for, and they will be without funds for a while, causing widespread anxiety. Letters and telegrams have been pouring in, and some directors of education have even traveled from afar to Beijing to appeal. Furthermore, educational organizations from various regions have been sending representatives to the ministry to call for action, urgently requesting the clarification of relief measures to prevent the current ongoing educational endeavors from being halted midway.

Previously, the Executive Yuan's Order No. 4252 stated that educational funding is essential for the vitality of schools, and the government should be responsible for planning to ensure that regular expenses are not lacking and that the fund is not shaken, so as not to hinder educational development and independence, etc. Indeed, education is a long-term plan and a fundamental undertaking of construction, which cannot be interrupted for a single day. Educational funding should continue to be guaranteed its independence to comply with the party's political platform. Now, to comply with the party platform, protect the independence of educational funding, and relieve the current educational crisis, the following measures are proposed: (1) Educational special funds allocated from national regular taxes or surtaxes, such as Lilkin and surcharges on salt, tobacco, and alcohol, etc., should be allocated by designated local national tax authorities according to the original approved amount before definite compensatory measures are determined, to avoid educational disruption. (2) Local special taxes that have long been designated for educational special funds, such as those with special characteristics that do not significantly conflict with the newly promulgated tax system, should be allowed to continue to be handled as before. If it is necessary to levy new taxes, the original plan should be consulted, and this tax revenue should still be allocated for educational funding. (3) Designated national tax authorities and other financial authorities should allocate local educational funding on a monthly basis to educational administrative agencies or educational funding management committees to avoid delays, arrears, and misappropriation.

The above measures are of great importance to the education of the entire province. The Ministry of Education has prepared this document and respectfully requests the Executive Yuan to review and instruct compliance. The Executive Yuan Secretariat replied that the Ministry of Education's submission regarding the draft measures to continue guaranteeing the independent funding of education after the abolition of Lilkin and unified salt tax was submitted for review. The case was brought up at the 11th National Affairs Conference of the Executive Yuan and, according to the first measure, the Ministry of Finance was ordered to handle it accordingly, and an order has been issued accordingly. You are hereby informed for your reference.

Jiangsu Province Slaughter and Teeth Taxes Still Handled by the Management Office 92

The case of Jiangsu Province's slaughter and teeth taxes still being handled by the education funding management office as before has been approved by the Ministry of Education and verified by the Ministry of Finance to be in accordance with the regulations. The Ministry of Education informed the Jiangsu Provincial Government that the Provincial Government and Education Funding Committee had consulted with the Ministry of Finance regarding the proposal to allocate the slaughter and teeth taxes, which are special education funds, after the reorganization of business taxes, and to have them continue to be handled by the Education Funding Management Office as before. This Ministry consulted with the Ministry of Finance, which replied that it was in accordance with the provisions of Article 11 of the Supplementary Measures to the General Outline of Business Tax Collection in Various Provinces. Therefore, in addition to the Ministry filing the case, you are hereby informed and requested to inform the Education Funding Committee accordingly.

The Portuguese have lost three goals in a row, and have reached the point where the mountains are exhausted and the water is gone. They made a final struggle to avoid total annihilation. Colasa took the lead and passed the ball to the right, taking the opportunity to enter directly. Zhou Xianyan撲地擒住,随手抛出, Chen Pu帶出重围, Colashi once again made a visit,发腿射门, the lone pillar弹地, Chen Jiaqiu救驾有功, and the龙门全保. As a result, China净胜 three goals.

New Chang Steamer of the China Merchants Bureau Runs Aground 125

▲ Near Saddle Island

▲ Due to Heavy Sea Fog

▲ Passengers Safe and Sound

The New Chang steamer of the China Merchants Bureau, en route from Dalian to Shantou, ran aground on the night of the 6th. While sailing near Saddle Island outside of Wusong, it suddenly encountered dense fog and heavy winds. The ship became stuck on the reef, with its hull wedged into the rocks. One of the cargo holds has already cracked. Upon receiving the news, the Shanghai office immediately began rescue efforts. The details of the accident, including the circumstances from beginning to end, are urgently investigated and recorded as follows:

Circumstances of the Accident: The New Chang steamer, loaded with 30,000 dan of soybeans and soybean cakes in Dalian, set sail from Dalian Bay on the 3rd of this month, heading directly for Shantou to unload. The journey was relatively calm until 7:30 PM on the 6th, when it reached a point 67 nautical miles from Wusong and 12 nautical miles east of Daji Mountain, near a place called Elliot Islands (Furu Mountain). The sea was foggy, and the wind and waves were extremely strong, with waves rising to a height of ten to fifteen feet. The ship was tossed about by the huge waves and became impossible to steer. Outside the Furu Mountain reefs, the water was swirling with immense suction. The New Chang steamer, with First Mate Zhao Shimei on duty, was hit by the violent wind and waves with a loud crash and ran aground on the Furu Mountain reefs. The bottom of the ship became wedged in the submerged reefs, rendering it unable to move.

▲ Circumstances of Running Aground: The New Chang ran aground at 7:15 PM on the 6th. At that time, the ship was being pulled by the swirling water, making it impossible to move. When it hit the submerged reefs, the area that became wedged was near the engine room. Seawater immediately began to enter, but fortunately, the bottoms of the cargo holds had not been breached.

Currently, there is no seawater in the cargo holds, but because the reef is stuck in the ship, the vessel cannot be moved, for fear that the bottom of the hold will be torn open by the rocks.

▲ Ship's Owner Asks for Help: The ship's owner, Soden, urgently sent an SOS wireless telegraph signal after the accident. The first to receive the message was the Italian mail steamer Ganji and the Lijin patrol ship of the Jianghai Customs. In accordance with the obligation to provide assistance in maritime disasters, the Italian mail steamer dispatched three motorboats to Furu Mountain Reef to rescue the crew of the New Chang. However, the wind and waves were too strong, and the three motorboats were unable to proceed. The Lijin patrol ship then dispatched a lifeboat to assist in the rescue. They first rescued 25 members of the ship's cargo handling staff, including Tang Rihua, and transferred them to the Yih Ho Yang Hang's Kuang Sheng steamer to be taken back to Shanghai.

▲ Shanghai Office Rescue Efforts: The Shanghai China Merchants Bureau received an urgent telegram from the New Chang steamer reporting the accident on the night of the 6th. Upon receiving the report, General Manager Li immediately ordered the shipping department to rush to handle the rescue work. He immediately ordered the Xinfeng and Kuangli steamers in Shanghai to fire up their engines and stand by for departure. However, after consideration, he decided that due to the strong wind and waves and the swift currents, it would not be appropriate to send large ships, as it could be dangerous. Therefore, he hired the Huidefeng large tugboat Xuepuxun, carrying machinery and food, to rush to the site of the accident to provide assistance. At the same time, he ordered the chief captain McKenna, first mate Gu Jiuquan, chief engineer Ying Xiaorong, engineer Zhang Yao, and helmsmen to board the tugboat and sail to the accident site to assess the situation and direct the rescue efforts.

Hai Yan Sets Sail: General Manager Li, considering that there were 112 crew members, sailors, and cargo escorts on board the New Chang steamer, telegraphed the Hai Yan steamer (returning to Shanghai from Wenzhou) and the Kuangda steamer (sailing from Shanghai to Shantou and Guangdong), which were traveling and closer to Saddle Island, to quickly change course to the site and join the rescue efforts, for the sake of the safety of the crew and passengers. Yesterday afternoon, the Shanghai office received a telegram stating that the Hai Yan steamer had arrived at the Saddle Island waters at 6 PM and was carrying out rescue work. The Jianghai Customs' Lijin ship had also arrived near Furu Mountain to assist in rescuing the crew.

▲ Crew Safety: The ship was sailing from Dalian this time and did not carry passengers, only five cargo escorts. All the crew members and sailors, except for the 25 members of the cargo handling department, including Lu Ji, Liang Ding, Mai Libao, Cao En, and Yu Gao, who were rescued by the Kuang Sheng steamer and arrived in Shanghai at 11 AM yesterday, reported the accident to the office. The office immediately arranged accommodation for these individuals. After the New Chang accident, more than 40 crew members temporarily sought refuge on Furu Mountain. Yesterday, the office received another telegram from the New Chang stating that all the crew members were safe and had been rescued onto the Lijin, Hai Yan, and Xuepuxun ships. They may all be transported back to Shanghai last night or today.

▲ Question of Responsibility: The accident was entirely due to fog and heavy wind and waves. The ship's owner, Soden, is British and has a wealth of experience and is known to be careful in the maritime industry. He has been working for the New Chang for more than a decade. He is familiar with the navigation routes in the North and South Seas and has never made a mistake. The first and second mates, Zhao Shimei and Sun Zhuoren, are also highly experienced. The grounding this time was truly an unpredictable natural disaster and an irresistible maritime accident. According to the Italian mail steamer owner, the New Chang accident was indeed impossible to prevent. He also said that the seawater in that area is swirling and the wind and waves are huge, and even large ships can hardly avoid such unexpected maritime accidents.

▲ Ship's Overview: The New Chang has a deadweight of 2,000 tons and was built in 1905. Its speed is 11 nautical miles per hour. The cabins are excellent, and the hull is very strong. It is the only excellent ship of the Bureau capable of sailing to Hong Kong. The ship is currently valued at 800,000 taels. This time, the submerged reef became wedged in the engine room. If seawater does not enter the cargo holds within 48 hours, it may still be possible to rescue it. However, it is said that some of the beans in one of the cargo holds have been soaked in water and have swelled, causing the hull to crack. Yesterday, the Bureau also telegraphed the Ministry of the Navy to send warships to protect the rescue ships and prevent pirates from looting. Currently, the New Chang is stranded on the reefs and has not shown any signs of sinking.

▲ Telegram to the National Government: To Chairman Chiang of the National Government in Nanjing: Late this evening, we received an urgent telegram from the New Chang steamer stating that it had run aground due to fog near Saddle Island outside of Wusong and requesting rescue. We immediately telegraphed the ships along the coast to rush to the rescue and urgently dispatched the Kuangda and Hai Yan steamers, which were the closest in terms of navigation, to return and assist in the rescue. At the same time, we hired additional tugboats and ordered the chief captain and engineers to lead the staff and workers, carrying food and clothing, to rush to meet them. The responsible officers worked through the night. We have now received confirmed reports from all parties stating that all the personnel on board have been safely evacuated and that 25 people have been transported back to the Bureau by the Yih Ho Kuang Sheng steamer. The rest will arrive later tonight. However, we have heard that the hull has cracked due to the beans and soybean cakes swelling upon contact with water. The New Chang was heading to Dalian to load goods and sailing directly to Shantou, which was very profitable in terms of business. The captain, an Englishman named Soden, and the first mate, Zhao Shimei, have both been serving on the ship for many years, are highly qualified, and have a wealth of experience. They were on duty together at the time of the accident. The reason for the accident will only be known in detail after the captain returns to the Bureau. I am writing to report this matter first, and further reports will follow. Your subordinate, Li Zhonggong, humbly reports.

International Women's Day Today 127

▲ Commemorative Meeting by the Municipal Women's Association

▲ Declaration of a Letter to Women

Today (8th) is the day when women in countries around the world seek equal liberation. The 8th of March, International Women's Day, is the most glorious and splendid page in the history of the women's movement. The Shanghai Women's Association has specially designated this morning at 9 AM to hold a commemorative meeting in the Association's auditorium. It is reported that in addition to posting slogans on trams, cars, and other vehicles, propaganda teams will be organized to give speeches along the way and to publish a letter to women on International Women's Day, the original text of which is copied below:

Dear sisters, on March 8, 1909, American women who were aware of the situation, because they were unwilling to accept social discrimination and unequal treatment, rose up to hold a great demonstration movement, in order to awaken women's self-liberation. Then, in 1910, when the International Women's Socialists met in the capital of Denmark, it was decided that March 8 would be International Women's Day. The following year, the women of Germany and the United States took the lead in commemorating it, holding large-scale mass demonstrations on "March 8." At the same time, in Vienna, Austria, more than 80,000 female workers participated. Their general demands were "Women's Suffrage" and "Protection of Female Workers," striving for absolute equality between men and women in politics, economics, and society. Later, the women of Britain and the Netherlands also held similar demonstrations. Thus, March 8 has been recognized by countries around the world as a day for international women's propaganda and unity, in order to seek equal liberation. During the World War, women in Western Europe rose up to organize demonstrations against the war, putting forward the slogans of "Bread" and "Peace" to fight for women's economic rights. Therefore, the words "March 8" awakened the obsessed women of East Asian countries and gave Asian women a lot of awareness and stimulation, especially in China. Therefore, "March 8" International Women's Day is really the most glorious and splendid page in the history of the women's liberation movement. Chinese women are subjected to the invasion of international imperialism and the oppression of feudal patriarchal forces, and their suffering is deeper and greater than that of women in Europe and the United States. Naturally, our desire for liberation is more urgent than that of women in Europe and the United States. Since the climax of the "March 8" commemoration was transmitted to China, Chinese women have automatically commemorated it in the same way as women around the world. This not only shows the awareness of Chinese women of their own suffering, but also deeply reflects the recognition and courage of women regarding the need for revolution. Furthermore, the Chinese women's liberation movement has its own special significance, that is, the Chinese women's liberation movement is related to the national revolution movement of the Chinese national liberation movement. The success of the Chinese National Revolution is the liberation of Chinese women, so Chinese women must work together with all the people for the National Revolution. Looking around at the current situation, the evil forces that shackle all women and bind all the people, namely the imperialists abroad and the feudal forces at home, are the targets of the National Revolution. Although they are gradually being eradicated, and at this time when the dawn of a new era is in sight, we feel that we should make further efforts to complete the unfinished success. Oppressed women, rise up! On this day of commemorating "March 8," prepare to rise up! We believe that if we rise up ourselves, we will have great power. We believe even more that only by rising up ourselves can we achieve true liberation. Our slogans are: (1) Commemorate the glorious and great "March 8," (2) Women unite under the leadership of the Chinese Kuomintang, (3) Eradicate feudal patriarchal forces, and (4) Down with imperialism.

Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau Orders the Prohibition of the Housheng Cotton Mill's Sale 128

▲ And Submits a Request to the Ministry of Industry for Instructions on How to Handle the Matter

Regarding the sale of the Housheng Cotton Mill to the Japanese-owned Gonda Cotton Mill, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has sent Tian Heqing, a staff member of the Second Section, to investigate. As the matter is indeed true, yesterday, the Bureau issued an order to the Housheng Mill, prohibiting the sale to the Japanese company, and submitted a report to the Ministry of Industry requesting instructions on how to handle the matter. The orders and reports are recorded below:

▲ Order to the Housheng Mill: For the purpose of complying with the order, the case of the mill's impending transfer to a Japanese company, as reported in the Textile Times, was previously ordered by this Bureau to refrain from signing contracts without the approval of this Bureau. Subsequently, the mill responded, stating that there was no sale to a Japanese company. However, on the 3rd of this month, various local newspapers reported that the mill had indeed been sold to the Gonda Cotton Mill. This Bureau sent staff to investigate in detail and inquired with the Gonda Cotton Mill, which admitted to the sale. It was also stated that on the 28th of last month and the 1st of this month, Xue Gansheng, a shareholder of the mill, accompanied Kurachi Shiro, the manager of the Gonda Cotton Mill, and more than ten staff members to the mill to inspect the machinery and measure the factory grounds. There was clear preparation for sale. It is noted that Japanese companies are seeking to establish factories in our country to monopolize the cotton yarn market due to the increase in import tariffs. All of our colleagues in the industry should strive to prevent this in order to save the situation. Even if the mill is unable to maintain itself, it should be transferred to Chinese individuals. However, the mill is not considering this and is acting willfully, selling our dying textile industry to a Japanese company and becoming a laughingstock in the industry, which is regrettable for the mill. Therefore, it is again ordered that the mill comply and immediately cancel any agreements or draft contracts agreed upon with the Gonda Cotton Mill within three days of receiving this order. If you dare to violate this order, you will be severely punished. This order is imperative.

▲ Report to the Ministry of Industry: For the purpose of reporting a matter, the Hua Shang Cotton Mill Federation issued the 768th issue of the Textile Times, stating that since the Housheng Cotton Mill ceased operations, there have been repeated rumors of a sale. It is said that Japanese companies such as Daikang Mill and Shanghai Mill have sent people to inspect and assess the value. Once an agreement is reached, it can be finalized. After this Bureau ordered the mill not to enter into any contracts without the approval of this Bureau, the mill responded, absolutely denying any sale to a Japanese company. However, recent rumors have spread that the mill has been sold to the Gonda Mill. Staff were sent to investigate the matter in detail. According to the report, the Housheng Cotton Mill suffered a loss of more than one million yuan last year due to the impact of soaring gold prices and poor internal management. Therefore, the mill did not intend to continue operating and repeatedly contacted Daikang Cotton Mill, Shanghai Cotton Mill, and Gonda Cotton Mill, Japanese companies, regarding a sale. On the 28th of last month and the 1st of this month, Xue Gansheng, a shareholder of the mill, led Kurachi Shiro, the manager of the Gonda Cotton Mill, and more than ten staff members to the Housheng Cotton Mill to inspect various parts of the machinery and measure the entire factory site. The Japanese companies did indeed have the intention to purchase. When inquiring with the Gonda Cotton Mill, Kawamura, the chief of the general affairs section of the mill, stated that the factory had indeed sent people to the Housheng Cotton Mill twice to inspect it, seemingly intending to buy it. However, a thorough investigation is still needed before reporting to the Japanese Gonda head office. Whether or not the transaction will take place depends on the decision of the head office and is unlikely to happen in the short term. Based on this, it is noted that the Housheng Mill is one of our Chinese-owned cotton mills. The mill has 70,000 yarn spindles and 1,400 weaving machines, with a total of 4,500 male and female workers. If it is sold to a Japanese company, not only will many workers lose their jobs, but the future of the spinning industry will also be affected. It is also noted that Japanese companies are seeking to expand their cotton yarn business in China due to the increase in import taxes. Our cotton textile industry should strive to prevent this. However, the Housheng Cotton Mill is selling its established business to a Japanese company, which is like inviting a wolf into the house and will cause endless harm. Furthermore, the shareholders of the mill, Xue Gansheng (son of Xue Baorun), Bei Runsheng, and Xi Hexian, all have huge personal assets, which should be more than enough to maintain the operation of the mill. Even if a transfer is absolutely necessary, it should be transferred to Chinese individuals first. Alternatively, the cotton mill industry could work together to maintain it, or the government could raise funds to buy it and convert it into a state-owned enterprise. All of these are possible. This matter concerns national welfare and the people's livelihood. In addition to this Bureau directly ordering the mill to comply with the previous order, the Bureau requests instructions from your honorable superiors on how to handle this matter. The circumstances are truthfully reported and respectfully submitted to your honorable superiors for review and guidance. This is a public matter. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Industry.

Japanese Fishing Boats Falsely Use Registration Numbers 129

▲ Discovered by the Customs Yellow Boat

▲ Four Vessels Confiscated

The Jianghai Customs Commissioner ordered the Jiang Patrol Officers (commonly known as "Yellow Boats") stationed at the Wusong Paotai Bay to require Japanese fishing boats to report to the Yellow Boat officers for inspection before entering Shanghai. Since the inspection began, the officers have discovered that only about 20 Japanese fishing boats have been registered with the customs, while the total number of Japanese fishing boats is about 100. When traveling in and out of port, they specifically use fake numbers to deceive the authorities. The officers have paid close attention to this during inspections. On the 26th of last month, the Daicheng Maru No. 12 and Daicheng Maru No. 13 fishing boats were found to be using fake numbers. The two vessels were detained and reported to the Customs Commissioner, who ordered the two vessels to be confiscated. Just as they were about to be auctioned, the Ryobo Maru and the Daiwa Maru, two Japanese fishing boats, suddenly came to communicate on the 5th of this month, conspiring to help the two Daicheng Maru escape. Fortunately, the Yellow Boat officers and crew discovered this and detained all four Japanese vessels for inspection. The Ryobo Maru and the Daiwa Maru also had informal numbers. This has been reported to the Customs Commissioner, who ordered that the four vessels be confiscated. It is also heard that Japanese fishing boats not only fish illegally in the waters of Zhejiang Province, but also have a habit of stealing silk cocoons, causing great harm to fishing boats and making it impossible for them to make a living. Because Japanese fishing boats are equipped with diesel engines, after the fishing boats cast their nets and the fish are full, the fishing boats only need to pass by the boat, and the fish and nets are swept away by the propellers. As a result, the boatmen suffer significant losses. They have submitted a petition to the relevant authorities in Zhejiang Province, requesting that they make serious representations to the Japanese side.

League of Nations Will Promote International Conference to Discuss Silver Prices 133

▲ Adopting Zhang Jiaao's Proposal

According to the Continental News, when the International Chamber of Commerce held an executive committee meeting in Paris a few days ago, Zhang Jiaao, the general manager of the Bank of China, sent a telegram to the meeting, proposing to convene an international silver price conference to discuss the issue of silver prices. Later, a few days ago, Mr. Zhang received a reply from Mr. Tolins, the general secretary of the meeting, stating that he was urging the national branches of the meeting to request their respective governments to immediately contact each other to convene an international conference. Private sources also indicated that Mr. Tolins's letter to the national branches was quite effective. It is expected that the diplomatic circles of various countries will soon exchange views. Yesterday, this port also received a private telegram from Geneva, stating that after receiving Mr. Zhang's telegram, the meeting immediately exchanged views with the League of Nations. It is now heard that the League of Nations is planning to adopt this suggestion. However, according to a certain important figure in this port, if such an international conference can be realized, at least one month of preparation is required before convening it. It is expected that Mr. Tolins's notification letter will be delivered to the Chinese branch in this port within the next week.

Customs to Refund Overcharged Cotton Yarn Tax 134

▲Two Replies from the Consolidated Tax Bureau

The Ministry of Finance's Consolidated Tax Bureau yesterday replied to the letter from the Chinese Cotton Mill Association, stating: "To the esteemed Association, your letter along with Mr. Zhou Xinbo's opinion paper has been received and carefully reviewed. The points you raised are not without merit. However, at the initial stage of implementing the consolidated tax, this Bureau had to strive for meticulousness in the tax collection procedures to ensure smooth execution. If businesses find it burdensome, any requests for changes will be carefully considered and improved to ensure both the tax policy and business interests are well-served. Regarding the Customs' continued collection of tariffs on goods that have already paid the consolidated tax, this Bureau received a letter from the Customs Administration yesterday, stating that the Inspector General of Customs has telegraphed instructions to all Customs offices to cease the collection and has stipulated that any cotton yarn tariffs collected after February 1st should be refunded upon presentation of the consolidated tax receipt. This Bureau has already copied the letter and notified your Association to inform relevant parties. It is expected that such issues will not arise again in the future. We hereby reply for your information and request that you forward this to Mr. Zhou of Zhentai Cotton Mill for his reference."

The Ministry of Finance's Consolidated Tax Bureau replied to the Cotton Cloth Industry Association: "To the esteemed Association, your letter has been received. Regarding the collection of export tariffs by various Customs offices on cotton yarn and cloth that have already paid the consolidated tax, this Bureau received a reply from the Customs Administration yesterday, stating that the Inspector General of Customs had telegraphed that the procedures for collecting the consolidated tax were finalized on the 20th of this month after thorough study and have been communicated to all Customs offices for compliance. The notification also stipulates that any cotton yarn tariffs collected after February 1st should be refunded upon presentation of the consolidated tax receipt. This has been communicated to the Bureau and forwarded to the Chinese Cotton Mill Association for notification on March 2nd. It is expected that there will be no further instances of repeated taxation or hindering transportation. We hereby reply for your information and request that you inform all businesses accordingly."

Various Industries Request Reduction in Business Tax 136

▲Restaurant Industry

Mr. Cheng Kefan, Standing Committee Member of the Shanghai Restaurant Industry Association, sent a letter to the Tax Rules Research Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday: "To the esteemed Committee, we have reviewed the Jiangsu Province Business Tax Regulations Draft and found that the business tax of 20 per mille (2%) for the restaurant industry, as specified in Article 4 and the tax rate table, exceeds the Ministry's established guideline by ten times, which is truly unbearable. The raw materials purchased by the restaurant industry daily, including dried goods, seafood, rice, flour, fish, meat, oil, salt, soy sauce, vinegar, chicken, duck, and various other ingredients, are all subject to tax. After being cooked and subjected to the business tax, we request a reduction in taxation [point one]. The government's decision to abolish likin and implement tax reform is admired by businesses and citizens. Business tax collection is a duty of citizens to supplement local finances. We earnestly request that the Jiangsu Province's proposed business tax standard, based on the Ministry's guideline of 1 to 2 per mille (0.1% to 0.2%), be applied to the restaurant industry, as the current 20 per mille (2%) is extremely difficult to bear. Our businesses cater specifically to the essential dining needs of merchants and customers, and a reduced tax rate of 1 per mille (0.1%) is particularly warranted [point two]. The circumstances within our area are unique, with separate Chinese and foreign concessions. The business tax must be implemented simultaneously in both concessions to avoid disputes among businesses. Most large restaurants are located in the concessions, and simultaneous implementation is necessary [point three]. In summary, we request that your Committee review and forward our concerns to the authorities, requesting a reduction in the business tax to 1 per mille (0.1%) and a revision of the taxable standards and tax rate table to adopt the principle of 'one item, one tax' to benefit the people's livelihood and alleviate the difficulties of businesses. We earnestly request that your Committee adopt our humble suggestions and conduct a study. We respectfully submit this letter with the hope that you will consider it. We are deeply grateful. (Remainder omitted)."

▲Woolen Fabric Industry

The Shanghai Woolen Fabric Industry Association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday: "To the esteemed Committee, we are dismayed by the 15 and 20 per mille (1.5% and 2%) tax rates on woolen fabrics in the draft business tax regulations issued by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. Our industry's woolen fabrics include all kinds of cotton and wool raw materials. In addition to Chinese and foreign woolen fabrics, we also deal in piece goods, hence the name 'woolen fabrics,' but it is not limited to wool and woolens alone. For example, the silk and satin industry primarily refers to silk and satin, but it also deals in woolen fabrics and foreign goods. Similarly, the foreign cloth industry mainly refers to cloth, but it also deals in woolen fabrics. In terms of industry nomenclature, there are names like silk and satin, foreign cloth, and woolen fabrics, but in actual business, the woolen fabric industry also deals in cloth, and the silk and satin and foreign cloth industries almost always deal in woolen fabrics. It is a mixed rather than a pure industry, and in the current business practice, it is impossible to separate them. Therefore, an equal tax rate should be applied to silk and satin, foreign cloth, and woolen fabrics [point one]. Regarding woolen fabrics themselves, with the increasing invention and sale of domestic products, they cannot all be considered expensive imports requiring regulation. Moreover, woolen fabrics are durable. In terms of value, many are equivalent to ordinary cotton cloth, and silk-like cotton cloth is one to two times more expensive than woolen fabrics. They are plain and unadorned, suitable for daily wear, and have become a common type of clothing that cannot be equated with luxury goods. When making clothes for ordinary people, not only is the price low, but the durability is also important, making woolen fabrics the first choice. Woolen fabrics are indeed necessities of life. Therefore, a light tax should be applied to woolen fabrics [point two]. However, the draft business tax regulations of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provincial Governments impose tax rates of 15 and 20 per mille (1.5% and 2%) on woolen fabrics, which are necessities of life. This not only contradicts the general guidelines but also fails to understand social conditions and the needs of the people. Therefore, the public is confused and there is a strong backlash. As this city is in the initial stage of drafting business tax regulations, we should consider both tax policies, business difficulties, social conditions, and people's livelihood. Therefore, we submit this letter detailing the situation of our industry. We earnestly request that your Committee forward it to the Municipal Government and the Ministry of Finance for detailed review, ensuring that the tax rate does not exceed 2 per mille (0.2%). If the tax rates set by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provincial Governments are adopted, it will not only deprive businesses of their livelihood but also endanger the capital of stores, leaving businesses and citizens without means of survival. In addition to sending representatives to submit our concerns in person, we are sending this letter in advance, hoping for your consideration."

▲Department Store Industry

The Shanghai Department Store Industry Association stated that the 10 per mille (1%) business tax set by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provincial Governments exceeds the maximum rate of the general guidelines by more than five times, making it unbearable. The tax rates are inconsistent and based on individual items. The industry sells nearly a thousand items, and future disturbances are inevitable. Therefore, Zheng Hairuo, Zhang Wei, Cheng Guichu, Zheng Chengqing, Chen Xiangqing, and other representatives were sent to Beijing the day before yesterday to petition. They arrived in Beijing yesterday morning and are staying at the Central Hotel. In the afternoon, they petitioned the National Government, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry.

News from the Eighth International Women's Association Conference 139

▲Held Once Every Five Years

According to diplomatic sources, the International Women's Association, since its inception in 1888, has stipulated that a conference be held once every five years, hence the name "Five-Year Conference." The Eighth Conference was held in Vienna, Austria, from May 29 to June 5, 1920, lasting eight days. Representatives from more than 40 countries attended, with over 600 members. The Chinese representative was Ms. Tang Baozhu, minister to Sweden and Norway. Although the conference lasted only eight days, more than 70 resolutions were passed, covering revisions to the association's constitution, as well as discussions on issues such as peace, education, law, health, women's occupation, and economy.

Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Close Qibao Branch Office 140

The Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau issued an instruction to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday: "For compliance, we have received Municipal Government Instruction No. 7389, which states: 'Approved Jiangsu Provincial Government Consultation No. 319 regarding this matter. According to a report from the Department of Construction, the Magistrate of Songjiang County, Jin Qingzhang, reported that the Chairman of the Xinzhuang Town Chamber of Commerce, Wang Zhaoyun, reported that the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce had established a branch office in Qibao Town, which is beyond its jurisdiction. Despite repeated negotiations by the local chamber of commerce, no resolution has been reached. The circumstances of the negotiation are submitted for your review. We request that the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau argue the case and forward it to the Provincial Department for instruction to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to close the branch office in order to uphold regional integrity and comply with the law.' Eight accompanying documents are attached. Accordingly, after investigation, Qibao Town has long been under the jurisdiction of the Xinzhuang Town Chamber of Commerce in Songjiang County. The scope of business branch offices should naturally be based on the original chamber of commerce boundaries, as clarified by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in Commercial Instruction No. 11256. Given the aforementioned circumstances, in addition to instructing and informing the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau to petition the Provincial Department for approval, we have copied the original attachments and submitted a special report for your review and guidance. According to Article 5 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, the area of a chamber of commerce shall be the administrative area of the city or county. Since the area of Qibao Town is provisionally excluded from the city's jurisdiction, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce should not establish a branch office there prematurely, as it will cause disputes. The aforementioned circumstances concern a matter of provincial and municipal administrative areas. In addition to instructing, we are reporting and requesting your review and instruction to order the closure of the branch office to avoid disputes and to receive your response.' Approved. Since Qibao Town is provisionally excluded from the city's jurisdiction, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce should not establish a branch office there prematurely, as it will cause disputes. Therefore, we request an investigation and instruction to close the branch office to prevent disputes and receive your response." It is reported that after receiving the order, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has forwarded it to Yang Xueqiao, director of the Qibao branch office, to comply with the order and close the office.

Proposal to Increase Tobacco Tax for Disaster Relief to be Postponed 141

The proposal to increase the cigarette tax to issue public bonds for disaster relief, after being submitted by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to the Executive Yuan and referred to the Ministry of Finance for review, has now been postponed by the Executive Yuan based on a petition from Bian Qihuan, a citizen of this city. The reasons given in the original petition are that China's economic situation, the environment of tobacco merchants, and the purchasing power of the people cannot be compared with those of Europe, America, and Japan. If this measure is implemented, disaster relief may not be achieved, and millions more Chinese merchants who rely on the tobacco industry will be harmed, giving foreign merchants an excellent opportunity to invade the market. Not only will the disaster relief bonds not be issued, but also the existing cigarette treasury bond fund will be shaken. It is also said that issuing public bonds for disaster relief is a fundamental mistake, and it is hoped that the government will not set this bad precedent. The petition lists the excessive issuance of public bonds and the excessive issuance of banknotes by various banks as the main reasons for the decline in the value of Chinese silver. These reasons were highly appreciated by the authorities, so the Executive Yuan instructed the Ministry of Finance to postpone the proposal based on these reasons. The letter from Xie Qi, Director of the Consolidated Tax Bureau, to Bian is as follows: "To Mr. Qihuan, I admire your insightful views. The case has been referred by the Ministry of Finance to the Executive Yuan, which has instructed that it be postponed. I am writing to inform you. [Signed] Xie Qi, Director of the Consolidated Tax Bureau."

Dispute Over Penalties Imposed by the French Concession Medical Board 144

▲Chinese Medical Association Sends Another Letter to the French Municipal Council

Since the implementation of doctor registration in the French Concession, penalties have been strictly enforced on unregistered doctors. The Chinese medical community believes that the deadline is too short, so the Shanghai Chinese Medical Association sent representatives to the French Municipal Council to lodge a serious protest. They met with Director-General Ai, who promised that the registration deadline would be extended to May 1, and that no penalties would be imposed on those who failed to register by May. On February 27, the Chinese Medical Association received an official letter from the French Municipal Council in French, stating that May 1 would be the deadline. This matter had been successfully negotiated and resolved. However, not long after, Huang Wenhua, a member of the Chinese Medical Association, was suddenly summoned by the French Municipal Council's Health Department the day before yesterday and fined two yuan. The Chinese Medical Association held a meeting to discuss the matter and sent another letter to the French Municipal Council, stating: "To the esteemed Director-General, regarding the regulations on doctors practicing in the Shanghai French Concession issued by your office, especially the articles on registration and fines, our Association has repeatedly raised three points, sent letters to your office, and sent representatives such as Xie Lixuan to request a solution from Director-General Huang. We were promised a solution and received a letter stating that the police had been instructed to refrain from inspections and penalties before May 1. The letter also stated that the regulations would be implemented on May 1, and all doctors, dentists, and veterinarians in the concession would be subject to these regulations. This was announced to the members of our Association in the French Concession. Not only is our Association grateful for your cooperation, but our members are also thankful. However, in recent days, many members in your concession have reported that your office is still urging them to register and imposing arbitrary fines, which is more severe than before. They have requested assistance from our Association. At first, we were skeptical, but on the 5th of this month, it was discovered that several members, including Huang Wenhua, had been fined, and the fine tickets were sent to our Association, which was shocking. It is believed that the implementation will begin on May 1. Since your Director-General had promised our representatives on February 15 and then sent a letter of approval on February 27, why are there arbitrary fines being issued on March 5? This seems to undermine the credibility of our Association and the prestige of your Director-General. Therefore, we are writing to request your Director-General to indicate how the fines imposed on several members for practicing without a license after February 15 will be handled, and whether there will be similar incidents by the police before May 1, so that our Association can explain to our members. We hope that you will investigate and reply."

▲More local news on the following page▲

Page 15

At nine o'clock on Tuesday evening, a man checked into the Yuegong Hotel, and the registration book recorded his name as Ma Yusun, from Beiping, 30 years old, working in politics, and arriving from Nanjing. That night, he and a woman shared room 26 on the fourth floor. The next day, this Mr. Ma suddenly told the cashier that his room was too small and not spacious enough, so he wanted to move to a larger one. On Wednesday evening, the two moved down a floor and changed to room 12 on the third floor. From that day on, the man and woman held hands and went out together, often returning late at night. The man wore a Zhongshan suit with an old-fashioned overcoat, while the woman wore a long blue Hua silk georgette qipao. Their clothes were ordinary and did not attract attention at first. However, every time they went out or returned, Ma Yusun would often nod and greet the staff at the cashier's desk. Sometimes the man and woman would go downstairs side by side, laughing and talking, looking very happy. The night before last, around eleven o'clock, Ma and his female companion, laughing and talking, went upstairs. The cashier asked Ma where he was coming from, and Ma replied, "We just came back from seeing a movie. Are you busy?" It was eleven o'clock at the time. After entering the room, Ma suddenly became enthusiastic and ordered a teaboy to summon a Cantonese prostitute to sing a song. The Cantonese song was mournful and moving, and the prostitute's voice was sweet and gentle. After the song ended, Ma applauded in admiration.

▲Writing a New Poem Before Death

The Yuegong Hotel's rules stipulate that teaboys ask guests at 3 PM each day if they wish to extend their stay. When the teaboy asked about room 12 on the third floor, there was no sound inside. The teaboy thought there was a female guest inside and did not dare to enter rashly, so he reported to the cashier for instructions. A certain Mr. Li, the cashier, was enthusiastic and feared something might have happened, so he told the teaboy to try to peek through the small window on the door. The teaboy followed the instructions and used a pole to move the curtains aside, and saw the couple lying motionless on the bed, looking pale. He quickly pried open the door and went inside to touch them. They were still breathing. He immediately hired a car to take them to Tongren Hospital for treatment and reported to the police station in the First District of the Fifth Precinct. The police station sent officers to investigate and found two suicide notes in room 12. One was addressed to the manager, saying, "We are borrowing this place to commit suicide, and we apologize profusely. There is no need for burial, we are grateful. [Signed] Ma Yusun, Bian Juefei." Bian was Ma's female companion. The other letter was addressed to "Gentlemen." Upon opening it, it was neither a letter nor a poem of seven-character quatrains or five-character ancient verse, but a modern poem. The original text is as follows:

The love in this world,

Is so painful,

Our bodies are burned for this,

To friends who sympathize with us,

Please do not be sad,

This is the vanguard of love,

Sorrow is the true meaning of love,

We wish you health,

We enclose our souls,

We bid you farewell,

Ma Yusun, Bian Juefei, written at the moment of death,

12:15, March 6, 1931.

Ma Yusun died shortly after arriving at the hospital, while Bian Juefei was in critical condition and also near death. As for the poison they took, it was thought to be an anesthetic powder, resembling icing sugar, wrapped in thin paper. A certain Mr. Li, out of curiosity, tasted it with his tongue and said that it was extremely bitter and he did not have the courage to swallow it.

Chinese Commercial Tramway 148

Misunderstandings After Resolution 149

▲ Yesterday morning all tram lines were suspended

▲ Service only resumed after 1 PM

Regarding the conflict between Chinese Commercial Tramway workers and naval aircraft artisans, the company's Route 4 and Route 1 trams were immediately shortened to South Railway Station. After mediation by various parties, a resolution was reached the night before last. Details were published in this newspaper. However, yesterday morning, due to the union's failure to issue a notification, the tram workers mistakenly believed the resolution had fallen through, and therefore did not report to work, resulting in the suspension of all Chinese Commercial Tramway lines in the southern city yesterday morning. It wasn't until they realized the situation and the union issued a notice ordering workers to return to work that service resumed around noon. Consequently, the vehicles did not leave the factory until after 1 PM. The details of the misunderstanding are recorded below:

▲ Resumption of Service: The day before yesterday, the Tramway Company and the Tramway Workers' Union, under the responsibility of Mayor Zhang Qun, accepted the three demands raised by the workers and issued a proclamation, immediately resuming service. Subsequently, as the Public Security Bureau required over a hundred copies of the proclamation and writing and printing took time, it was not delivered to the company until 8 PM. At that time, Wang Zijing, the Second District Chief of the Public Security Bureau, also led fifty members of the security team to maintain order in the Gaochang Temple area. However, the union's staff and standing directors had left for the night. With only a little over two hours remaining before the tram entered the factory, the workers, seeing the proclamation and the police maintaining order, immediately resumed service, reaching Gaochang Temple, effectively restoring normal operations.

▲ Yesterday Morning's Misunderstanding: The next morning, the union staff had to arrive after 8 AM. Furthermore, the workers who worked the previous night and those who worked the following morning had not met. Until yesterday morning, the union believed that since service had resumed the previous night, the following morning would be normal. However, the workers, seeing that the trams had resumed service last (the day before yesterday) night, but due to the lack of time, no notice had been issued, wondered why no notice had appeared this morning, leading to suspicion and the belief that negotiations had broken down. Consequently, they delayed reporting to the factory, and vehicles could not depart as usual. Upon realizing the situation, the Social Bureau sent Xu Zhi from the Third Section, Wang Zijing, the Second District Chief of the Public Security Bureau, and Officer Niu to the company to investigate the true reason for the suspension. The company was also summoning the union's standing committee members Zhu Hanhe, Zhou Guangrong, Fang Ronggen, and Xu Wangsheng for questioning. It was then discovered that the suspension was due to a misunderstanding. The union's standing committee immediately issued a notice, and vehicles only resumed normal service after 1 PM. Maintaining Order: After the trams on Routes 1 and 4 resumed direct service to Gaochang Temple, the Public Security Bureau's security team dispatched a total of fifty officers, divided into shifts of twenty-five, patrolling in sections. Eight officers were stationed in front of the Tramway Company's gate, eight in front of Gaochang Temple, and the rest accompanied the trams to provide protection. The deployment is expected to be withdrawn after today and tomorrow.

▲ Retaining Negotiation: While tram service has resumed, the injured tram workers remain in the hospital, and their injuries have not improved. Therefore, the union's standing committee members Zhu Hanhe and others, when meeting with Manager Lu Bohong at the company yesterday morning, requested preferential treatment for the injured and insisted on serious negotiations regarding the perpetrators to bring them to justice in the local court. Lu agreed to do his best to proceed with the matter.

▲ Service Resumption Notice: Yesterday, to explain the misunderstanding, the union issued a notice, stating: "Regarding the notice, our members, after being assaulted, abandoned the route. Yesterday, thanks to the Mayor's order, the Public Security Bureau issued a proclamation to ensure safety. Unexpectedly, the union did not see the proclamation issued until 8 PM last night. By the time the proclamation arrived, there were no responsible personnel at the union, which led to a misunderstanding and the cessation of work this morning. Now that the misunderstanding has been explained, we hope that all members will abide by the order and restore the original route traffic. We will continue to pursue subsequent matters. This is the notice."

Another Accomplice Found in the Assassination of Chen Qimei 150

▲ It is Wu Baoxian, sentenced to ten years

▲ Described the Incident in Court Yesterday

It has been fifteen years since the assassination of Mr. Chen Qimei. The case was reopened and attracted attention from both the government and the public after Nie Dianbang (also known as Nie Zhenbang) was arrested in Shanghai on January 6. Chairman Chiang ordered the Shanghai court to transfer Nie to Beijing and instructed Chen Enpu, a military judge from the General Headquarters, to come to Shanghai to investigate the evidence for review and handling. Later, it was heard that the case did not require military trial, so Nie was transferred from the General Headquarters to the Jiangning District Court for investigation and prosecution according to law. Now, the Jiangning Court learned that Nie had an accomplice, Wu Baoxian from Jingjiang, who had committed another theft case and was sentenced to ten years in prison by the Special District Court and imprisoned in the Tilanqiao Prison. Therefore, it sent a letter to the Special Court requesting a nearby inquiry. Yang, the President of the Special Court, notified the police. Yesterday morning, Wu was brought from the prison to the First Court. A witness was summoned. After being questioned by Judge Xu Jiashi, the witness stated that he used to live in Xinmin Lane on Avenue Joffre and was a neighbor of Chen Qimei. At 4 PM on May 18, he suddenly heard gunshots. He quickly went out to see that the defendants Wu Baoxian and Nie Dianbang were each holding a pistol and running out of Chen's residence. As they approached him, they shouted, "Get out of the way!" Before the incident, Nie and Wu often came to his shop to chat, so he knew them. He believed that their intention in coming to the shop was to gather information to take action when the opportunity arose. After the interrogation, Judge Xu instructed Wu Baoxian to be sent back to prison and to reply to the Jiangning District Court according to the situation for review and handling.

Fierce Competition Among Taxi Companies 151

▲ Lowering prices to attract customers; gasoline is expensive

▲ Five companies have closed since March

▲ Foreign firms reap the benefits

There are more than 120 taxi companies with over 1,100 taxis for hire in this city. Competition among them has always been fierce, but never as much as in the past three months. Now, the taxi companies are fighting each other like snipes and clams, while foreign taxi companies reap the benefits. Smaller companies have been affected by the competition and have been closing down one after another. The following is based on investigations conducted by the Daily News reporter from various sources:

▲ Cause of Competition: Of the more than 120 taxi companies in the city, less than half have strong capital. Most of the smaller companies pay only 20% of the price when purchasing cars from foreign firms, with the remaining 80% paid in monthly installments. However, the terms of the contract are very harsh. If a company cannot pay off the installments on time, the foreign firm will take back the car. Therefore, the only hope for companies that have purchased cars is to attract customers, develop their business, and pay off the outstanding installments on time. Thus, the practice of lowering prices to attract customers and competition among companies gradually arose.

▲ Gradually Intensifying: In mid-November last year, as gasoline prices gradually increased, it became difficult for companies to maintain competitiveness. The preparatory meeting of the Taxi Industry Association resolved two items: (1) to advise companies to stop competing by lowering prices; (2) to raise the price of taxi fares uniformly, such as raising the price of a ride that costs one yuan to 1.5 yuan, and raising the price of a chartered car from three yuan per hour to four yuan. However, a few companies did not implement this resolution, and the larger Huang Taxi Company also joined the competition, continuing to charge the old prices. Members once advised them, but the matter was not resolved. Therefore, Yunfei Taxi Company, a standing committee member of the preparatory meeting of the industry association, joined the fray, and competition became even more intense.

▲ Foreigners Reaping the Benefits: Since the beginning of December last year until now, Huang Taxi Company and Yunfei Taxi Company have been competing fiercely, and it has not stopped. Seeing that gold prices are rising daily and that taxi companies are competing with each other, the sales volume of gasoline in Shanghai has also increased daily. Therefore, they continue to raise prices, reaping the benefits. For example, the total amount of gasoline needed in Shanghai each month is more than 500,000 gallons. Last year, the lowest price per gallon was 41 cents, but now it has risen to 1.25 yuan per gallon. However, the price of taxi fares has been raised by smaller companies, while larger companies remain the same. Business losses are inevitable.

▲ Closing Down One After Another: For the sake of competing in business, larger companies keep their fares the same. Smaller companies have no choice but to implement the previous resolution of the industry association and raise prices, but business is slow, and losses are even greater. Therefore, since March, five companies have been affected by the competition and have closed down: Meili on Pingliang Road, Huaqiao on North Sichuan Road, Shunda, Sanxing on Avenue Edward VII, and Fuxing. There are still more than 40 companies that are barely surviving despite significant losses. If competition continues, they will also be severely affected and close down one after another.

▲ Final Mediation: Seeing that members are fighting like snipes and clams again, which will lead to complete destruction and mutual harm, the preparatory meeting of the industry association decided to convene a meeting of all members in the next few days to discuss and make a final mediation, first to unify the prices of taxi fares, agree on appropriate penalties for violators, and then seek the development of the future of the industry.

Giving Birth After Ten Years of Pregnancy 152

▲ The baby is smaller than normal

▲ The world is full of wonders

A resident surnamed Chen, from Zhenhai, Zhejiang, living at No. 439 and a half, Hele Lane, North Henan Road, is nearly sixty years old. He married a wife surnamed Mou more than twenty years ago but had never had children. Ten years ago, she suddenly became pregnant, and her abdomen grew daily. However, year after year, she did not give birth. Counting on fingers, it has been ten years. Finally, the other day (the fourth of this month), she suddenly went into labor and gave birth to a son. The baby is smaller than normal, seemingly premature. It is truly a strange story.

Assassination of Inspector An Involves the Owner of Liangxi Inn 156

▲ Li Maolin Firmly Denies

▲ Sentence of Temporary Detention; Rescheduled for Further Interrogation

Detectives from the Municipal Public Security Bureau arrested seven thieves who developed electric guns on the evening of the 5th in Yongqing Lane near Xiaobeimen. Page 16

Jiuchang and Dongbaochang Settle Lawsuit 160

Bao Chengliang, Dong Shengzheng, Tongyu, and others operating a fruit and local goods business at No. 16 Pu. The location of the business was originally the property of the China Merchants Bureau and was leased by Jiuchang Company. The company thus exercised its rights as the landlord. The business feared that the location would be taken by others, and they would lose their place of business. Therefore, the tenants united to form Dongbaochang Jingzu Chenfang and leased the entire property from Jiuchang Company. However, according to the lease terms, the tenants were obligated to invest in construction. In the 17th year of the Republic of China, the Municipal Government renovated Fangbang Middle Road and Qingshui Road. The location of the business was directly affected and workers were hired to renovate it. However, they had to pay 25,000 yuan for the road construction fee to the Municipal Finance Bureau. This road construction fee should have been paid by the landlord, the China Merchants Bureau. However, they delayed payment, so the Jingzu Chenfang paid it on their behalf and deducted it from the rent owed to Jiuchang Company. After it was deducted, Jiuchang Company suddenly refused to recognize the road construction fee and filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai District Court against Dongbaochang for rent arrears, demanding termination of the lease. Dongbaochang and the tenants also suffered significant losses as the new house had just been completed. They hired lawyers and filed a counterclaim. The court has repeatedly summoned them, and they have now settled in court. Here is a record of the settlement: Jiangsu Shanghai District Court Settlement Record: Plaintiff: Jiuchang Company; Legal Representative: Wang Shiqiang; Lawyer: Lu Shaozong; Defendant: Dongbaochang Jingzu Zhangfang: Zheng Feizhang, Sun Shiyuan, Dong Chunxue; Agents: Zheng Gengyu, Zhou Xiaoan, Zhu Sifu; Regarding the case of breach of contract between the parties listed above, the content of the settlement reached by the court in court (1) Both parties acknowledge that the lease contract signed between Jiuchang Company and Dongbaochang on the 29th day of the month in the 17th year of the Republic of China is valid. The agent of Jiuchang Company also acknowledges that the request for termination will be withdrawn immediately. (2) The road construction fee of 25,000 yuan should be borne by the landlord, China Merchants Bureau, according to the defendant's claim. Now the agent of the plaintiff, representing the plaintiff, acknowledges to advance 15,000 yuan, which will be deducted from the 25,000 yuan advanced by the defendant. The defendant's agent also represents the defendant to advance 10,000 yuan. Both parties will jointly negotiate with the China Merchants Bureau. All expenses will be borne equally by both parties. Regardless of the situation, both parties must cooperate and must not shirk responsibility. (3) The 6,324 yuan paid by the defendant to the Municipal Government for the coupon tax rent for November 12 of the 19th year of the Republic of China is approved by the plaintiff's agent on behalf of the plaintiff to be deducted from the rent owed. However, the defendant must also deliver the aforementioned receipt to the plaintiff before March 24. If the receipt is insufficient, cash should be paid according to the amount. (4) The rent requested by the plaintiff, from January 16 of the 19th year of the Republic of China to February 15 of the 20th year of the Republic of China, totals thirteen months, totaling 41,106 yuan. In addition to the 15,000 yuan for the road construction fee advanced by the plaintiff and the 6,324 yuan for the borrowed coupon tax rent, the amount due is 19,782 yuan, which must be paid in full before March 24 without delay. (9) The plaintiff acknowledges that the interest on the rent arrears, the defendant acknowledges that the interest on the advance payment, and other losses before the litigation are waived by both parties and will not be pursued. (6) The litigation costs of this case shall be borne by each party.

The Contribution of the Savings Department of the China National Bank 165

▲ Issuing Type B Gift Certificates

The Savings Department of the China National Bank has previously issued Type A gift certificates. In addition to being redeemable for cash at the bank's head office and branches in Shanghai, Suzhou, Nanjing, and Guangdong, they can also be used to purchase goods at full face value at the Sincere, Wing On, and Sun Sun department stores. Recently, as the savings business of commercial firms has not been legalized and is still in a state of suspension, it is convenient to use the China National Bank's gift certificates to pay when shopping at major companies to avoid carrying cash.
